Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry := range metadata {\n561: \t\tmm = append(mm, prompb.MetricMetadata{\n562: \t\t\tMetricFamilyName: entry.MetricFamily,\n563: \t\t\tHelp:             entry.Help,\n564: \t\t\tType:             prompb.FromMetadataType(entry.Type),\n565: \t\t\tUnit:             entry.Unit,\n566: \t\t})\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tpBuf := proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n570: \tnumSends := int(math.Ceil(float64(len(metadata)) / float64(t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n571: \tfor i := range numSends {\n572: \t\tlast := min((i+1)*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, len(metadata))\n573: \t\terr := \t\t\tt.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error while sending metadata\", \"count\", last-(i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend), \"err\", err)\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: }\n580: \n581: func (t *QueueManager) sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := func(try int) error {\n591: \t\tctx, span := otel.Tracer(\"\").Start(ctx, \"Remote Metadata Send Batch\")\n592: \t\tdefer span.End()\n593: \n594: \t\tspan.SetAttributes(\n595: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"metadata\", metadataCount),\n596: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"try\", try),\n597: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_name\", t.storeClient.Name()),\n598: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_url\", t.storeClient.Endpoint()),\n599: \t\t)\n600: \t\t// Attributes defined by OpenTelemetry semantic conventions.\n601: \t\tif try > 0 {\n602: \t\t\tspan.SetAttributes(semconv.HTTPResendCount(try))\n603: \t\t}\n604: \n605: \t\tbegin := time.Now()\n606: \t\t// Ignoring WriteResponseStats, because there is nothing for metadata, since it's\n607: \t\t// embedded in v2 calls now, and we do v1 here.\n608: \t\t_, err := t.storeClient.Store(ctx, req, try)\n609: \t\tt.metrics.sentBatchDuration.Observe(time.Since(begin).Seconds())\n610: \n611: \t\tif err != nil {\n612: \t\t\tspan.RecordError(err)\n613: \t\t\treturn err\n614: \t\t}\n615: \t\treturn nil\n616: \t}\n617: \n618: \tretry := func() {\n619: \t\tt.metrics.retriedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n620: \t}\n621: \terr = t.sendWriteRequestWithBackoff(ctx, attemptStore, retry)\n622: \tif err != nil {\n623: \t\treturn err\n624: \t}\n625: \tt.metrics.metadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n626: \tt.metrics.metadataBytesTotal.Add(float64(len(req)))\n627: \treturn nil\n628: }\n629: \n630: func isSampleOld(baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration, ts int64) bool {\n631: \tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n632: \t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n633: \t\treturn false\n634: \t}\n635: \tlimitTs := baseTime.Add(-sampleAgeLimit)\n636: \tsampleTs := timestamp.Time(ts)\n637: \treturn sampleTs.Before(limitTs)\n638: }\n639: \n640: func isTimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n641: \treturn func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n642: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n643: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n644: \t\t\treturn false\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tswitch {\n647: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n648: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n649: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Samples[0].Timestamp) {\n650: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n651: \t\t\t\treturn true\n652: \t\t\t}\n653: \t\tcase len(ts.Histograms) > 0:\n654: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, \t\t\t}\n663: \t\tdefault:\n664: \t\t\treturn false\n665: \t\t}\n666: \t\treturn false\n667: \t}\n668: }\n669: \n670: func isV2TimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n671: \treturn func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n672: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n673: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we Blocks until all samples are\n701: // enqueued on their shards or a shutdown signal is received.\n702: func (t *QueueManager) Append(samples []record.RefSample) bool {\n703: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n704: outer:\n705: \tfor _, s := range samples {\n706: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), s.T) {\n707: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n711: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[s.Ref]\n712: \t\tif !ok {\n713: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[s.Ref]; !ok {\n714: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped sample for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", s.Ref)\n715: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n716: \t\t\t} else {\n717: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n718: \t\t\t}\n719: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n720: \t\t\tcontinue\n721: \t\t}\n722: \t\t// TODO(cstyan): Handle or at least log an error if no metadata is found.\n723: \t\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n724: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[s.Ref]\n725: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n726: \t\t// Start with a very small backoff. This should not be t.cfg.MinBackoff\n727: \t\t// as it can happen without errors, and we want to pickup work after\n728: \t\t// filling a queue/resharding as quickly as possible.\n729: \t\t// TODO: Consider using the average duration of a request as the backoff.\n730: \t\tbackoff := model.Duration(5 * time.Millisecond)\n731: \t\tfor {\n732: \t\t\tselect {\n733: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n734: \t\t\t\treturn false\n735: \t\t\tdefault:\n736: \t\t\t}\n737: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{\n738: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels: lbls,\n739: \t\t\t\tmetadata:     meta,\n740: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:    s.T,\n741: \t\t\t\tvalue:        s.V,\n742: \t\t\t\tsType:        tSample,\n743: \t\t\t}) {\n744: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n745: \t\t\t}\n746: \n747: \t\t\tt.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n748: \t\t\ttime.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n749: \t\t\tbackoff *= 2\n750: \t\t\t// It is reasonable to use t.cfg.MaxBackoff here, as if we have hit\n751: \t\t\t// the full backoff we are likely waiting for external resources.\n752: \t\t\tif backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n753: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n754: \t\t\t}\n755: \t\t}\n756: \t}\n757: \treturn true\n758: }\n759: \n760: func (t *QueueManager) AppendExemplars(exemplars []record.RefExemplar) bool {\n761: \tif !t.sendExemplars {\n762: \t\treturn true\n763: \t}\n764: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n765: outer:\n766: \tfor _, e := \t\t\tcontinue\n770: \t\t}\n771: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n772: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[e.Ref]\n773: \t\tif !ok {\n774: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[e.Ref]; !ok {\n775: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n777: \t\t\t} else {\n778: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n779: \t\t\t}\n780: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n781: \t\t\tcontinue\n782: \t\t}\n783: \t\tmeta := {\n789: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n790: \t\t\t\treturn false\n791: \t\t\tdefault:\n792: \t\t\t}\n793: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(e.Ref, timeSeries{\n794: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels:   lbls,\n795: \t\t\t\tmetadata:       meta,\n796: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:      e.T,\n797: \t\t\t\tvalue:          e.V,\n798: \t\t\t\texemplarLabels: e.Labels,\n799: \t\t\t\tsType:          tExemplar,\n800: \t\t\t}) {\n801: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n802: \t\t\t}\n803: \n804: \t\t\tt.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n805: \t\t\ttime.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n806: \t\t\tbackoff *= 2\n807: \t\t\tif backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n808: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n809: \t\t\t}\n810: \t\t}\n811: \t}\n812: \treturn true\n813: }\n814: \n815: func (t *QueueManager) AppendHistograms(histograms \treturn true\n867: }\n868: \n869: func (t *QueueManager) AppendFloatHistograms(floatHistograms []record.RefFloatHistogramSample) bool {\n870: \tif !t.sendNativeHistograms {\n871: \t\treturn true\n872: \t}\n873: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n874: outer:\n875: \tfor _, h := range floatHistograms {\n876: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), h.T) {\n877: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n878: \t\t\tcontinue\n879: \t\t}\n880: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n881: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[h.Ref]\n882: \t\tif !ok {\n883: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[h.Ref]; !ok {\n884: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped histogram for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", h.Ref)\n885: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n886: \t\t\t} else {\n887: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n890: \t\t\tcontinue\n891: \t\t}\n892: \t\tmeta := \t\t\t\treturn false\n900: \t\t\tdefault:\n901: \t\t\t}\n902: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(h.Ref, timeSeries{\n903: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels:   lbls,\n904: \t\t\t\tmetadata:       meta,\n905: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:      h.T,\n906: \t\t\t\tfloatHistogram: h.FH,\n907: \t\t\t\tsType:          tFloatHistogram,\n908: \t\t\t}) {\n909: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n910: \t\t\t}\n911: \n912: t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n917: \t\t\t}\n918: \t\t}\n919: \t}\n920: \treturn true\n921: }\n922: \n923: // Start the queue manager sending samples to the remote storage.\n924: // Does not block.\n925: func (t *QueueManager) Start() {\n926: \t// Register and initialise some metrics.\n927: \tt.metrics.register()\n928: \tt.metrics.shardCapacity.Set(float64(t.cfg.Capacity))\n929: \tt.metrics.maxNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxShards))\n930: \tt.metrics.minNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n931: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n932: \tt.metrics.maxSamplesPerSend.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend))\n933: \n934: \tt.shards.start(t.numShards)\n935: \tt.watcher.Start()\n936: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n937: and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This\n954: \t// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which\n955: \t// causes a closed channel panic.\n956: \tt.shards.stop()\n957: \tt.watcher.Stop()\n958: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n959: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Stop()\n960: \t}\n961: \tt.metrics.unregister()\n962: }\n963: \n964: // StoreSeries keeps track of which series we know about for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n969: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n970: \tfor _, s := range series {\n971: \t\t// Just make sure all the Refs of Series will insert into seriesSegmentIndexes map StoreMetadata(meta []record.RefMetadata) {\n988: \tif t.protoMsg == config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n989: \t\treturn\n990: \t}\n991: \n992: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n993: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n994: \t}\n1001: }\n1002: \n1003: // UpdateSeriesSegment updates the segment number held against the series,\n1004: // so we can trim older ones in SeriesReset.\n1005: func (t *QueueManager) UpdateSeriesSegment(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1006: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1007: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1008: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1009: \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. WAL Watcher should have\n1014: // stored series records with the checkpoints index number, so we can now\n1015: // delete any ref ID's lower than that # from the two maps.\n1016: func (t *QueueManager) SeriesReset(index int) {\n1017: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1018: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1019: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1020: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1021: \t// Check for series that are in segments older than the checkpoint\n1022: \t// that were not also present in the checkpoint.\n1023: \tfor k, v := range t.seriesSegmentIndexes {\n1024: \t\tif v < index {\n1025: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesSegmentIndexes, k)\n1026: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesLabels, k)\n1027: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesMetadata, k)\n1028: \t\t\tdelete(t.droppedSeries, k)\n1029: \t\t}\n1030: \t}\n1031: }\n1032: \n1033: // SetClient updates the client used by a queue. Used when only client specific\n1034: // fields are updated to avoid restarting the queue.\n1035: func (t *QueueManager) SetClient(c WriteClient) {\n1036: \tt.clientMtx.Lock()\n1037: \tt.storeClient = c\n1038: \tt.clientMtx.Unlock()\n1039: }\n1040: \n1041: func (t *QueueManager) client() WriteClient {\n1042: \tt.clientMtx.RLock()\n1043: \tdefer t.clientMtx.RUnlock()\n1044: \treturn t.storeClient\n1045: }\n1046: \n1047: // processExternalLabels merges externalLabels into b. If b contains\n1048: // a label in externalLabels, the value in b wins.\n1049: func processExternalLabels(b *labels.Builder, externalLabels []labels.Label) {\n1050: \tfor _, el := range externalLabels {\n1051: \t\tif b.Get(el.Name) == \"\" {\n1052: \t\t\tb.Set(el.Name, el.Value)\n1053: \t\t}\n1054: \t}\n1055: }\n1056: \n1057: func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n1058: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64\n1217: \tenqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64\n1218: \n1219: \t// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you\n1220: \t// cannot select on a wait group.\n1221: \tdone    chan struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown    atomic.Uint32\n1231: \texemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown  atomic.Uint32\n1232: \thistogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown atomic.Uint32\n1233: \tmetadataDroppedOnHardShutdown   atomic.Uint32\n1234: }\n1235: \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = newQueue(s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, s.qm.cfg.Capacity)\n1247: \t}\n1248: \n1249: \ts.queues = newQueues\n1250: \n1251: \tvar hardShutdownCtx context.Context\n1252: \thardShutdownCtx, s.hardShutdown = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n1265: \t}\n1266: }\n1267: \n1268: // stop the shards; subsequent call to enqueue will return false.\n1269: func (s *shards) stop() {\n1270: \t// Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\t\treturn false\n1323: \t\t}\n1324: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1325: \t\tcase tSample:\n1326: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1327: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1328: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1329: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()\n1330: \t\t\ts.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()\n1331: \t\tcase tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:\n1332: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()\n1333: \t\t\ts.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()\n1334: \t\tdefault:\n1335: \t\t\treturn true\n1336: \t\t}\n1337: \t\ts.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))\n1338: \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n1361: \tmetadata       *metadata.Metadata\n1362: \ttimestamp      int64\n1363: \texemplarLabels labels.Labels\n1364: \t// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.\n1365: \tsType seriesType\n1366: }\n1367: \n1368: type seriesType int\n1369: \n1370: const (\n1371: \ttSample seriesType = iota\n1372: \ttExemplar\n1373: \ttHistogram\n1374: \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),\n1387: \t\tbatchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),\n1388: \t\t// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for\n1389: \t\t// the batch being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1411: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1412: \t\t\treturn false\n1413: \t\t}\n1414: \t}\n1415: \treturn true\n1416: }\n1417: \n1418: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1419: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1420: }\n1421: \n1422: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1423: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1424: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1425: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1426: \tselect {\n1427: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1428: \t\treturn batch\n1429: \tdefault:\n1430: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1431: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1432: \t\treturn batch\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1437: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1438: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1439: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1440: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1441: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1442: \t}\n1443: }\n1444: \n1445: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. No appends can be\n1446: // made after this is called.\n1447: func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n1448: \tfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n1449: \t\ttime.Sleep(time.Second)\n1450: \t}\n1451: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1452: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1453: \tq.batch = nil\n1454: \tclose(q.batchQueue)\n1455: }\n1456: \n1457: // tryEnqueueingBatch tries to send a batch if necessary. If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1462: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1463: \t\treturn false\n1464: \t}\n1465: \n1466: \tselect {\n1467: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1468: \t\treturn false\n1469: \tcase <-done:\n1470: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1471: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1472: \t\treturn false\n1473: \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = q.batchPool[:batches-1]\n1486: \t\treturn batch\n1487: \t}\n1488: \treturn make([]timeSeries, 0, capacity)\n1489: }\n1490: \n1491: func (s *shards) runShard(ctx context.Context, shardID int, queue *queue) {\n1492: \tdefer func() {\n1493: \t\tif s.running.Dec() == 0 {\n1494: \t\t\tclose(s.done)\n1495: \t\t}\n1496: \t}()\n1497: \n1498: \tshardNum := strconv.Itoa(shardID)\n1499: \tsymbolTable := \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Sub(float64(droppedHistograms))\n1572: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n1573: \n1604: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1605: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, sendSamplesWithBackoff to the remote storage with backoff for recoverable errors.\n1698: func (s *shards) sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_011DBve6teFYvPooTBQaMMSr","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the runShard function. It's a goroutine that:\n1. Receives batches from batchQueue (line 1580)\n2. Sends them via sendBatch (line 1585)\n3. Returns the batch for reuse (line 1588)\n4. Also has a timeout that sends partial batches (line 1593-1599)\n\nLet me now look at the issue more carefully. When resharding happens:\n1. reshardLoop calls t.shards.stop() to stop the old shards\n2. stop() closes softShutdown to signal no more enqueues\n3. stop() then takes the write lock and calls FlushAndShutdown on all queues\n4. Then reshardLoop calls t.shards.start(numShards) to start new shards\n\nThe critical issue I see is that when stop() closes softShutdown and then takes the write lock to call FlushAndShutdown, if a This is the bug!\n\nHere's the race condition that causes stalling shards:\n\n1. Old shards have some samples in flight (say, 100 samples enqueued)\n2. pendingSamples metric is at 100\n3. updateShardsLoop detects it should reshard and sends new number of shards to reshardChan\n4. reshardLoop calls stop() on old shards\n5. stop() closes softShutdown and calls FlushAndShutdown on all queues\n6. New shards are started and immediately start receiving new samples\n3. But what happens to the old shards that haven't finished flushing?\n\nThe issue is that when stop() is called, it waits for all shards to finish and triggers the \"done\" signal. \n\nThe stop() function spawns FlushAndShutdown as goroutines for each queue and waits for completion with a timeout. But there's a critical race: when FlushAndShutdown is running concurrently with runShard still processing batches, a batch sent to batchQueue could be received and processed by runShard before the shutdown completes.\n\nIf runShard then tries to send a new partial batch while the queue is full, both FlushAndShutdown and runShard could block indefinitely on channel sends—a deadlock scenario. The test TestQueue_FlushAndShutdownDoesNotDeadlock addresses this by ensuring queue.Batch() doesn't block forever even when FlushAndShutdown holds the lock, as indicated by the comment at line 1798.\n\nThe intermittent stalling suggests a race condition between old shards completing their flush, new shards receiving samples, and reshardLoop calling start() to reset pendingSamples. When tracing through enqueue() at line 1312, the function acquires a read lock and retrieves the appropriate shard based on the reference, but the timing of when samples are tracked versus when shards transition could cause some samples to be lost or delayed. waits for all queues to signal done. There's a potential race condition: between closing softShutdown and acquiring the write lock, in-flight enqueues that already passed the shutdown check will still increment pendingSamples. However, FlushAndShutdown should handle sending those samples.\n\nBut looking at start() again—it resets pendingSamples to 0 at line 1241, yet the old shards are still flushing their samples. If those shards decrement the metric via updateMetrics while the new instance is running, the counter gets corrupted.\n\nThe actual problem appears to be in the resharding sequence itself. The issue is clear now at line 1241: when start() is called to initialize new shards, it RESETS pendingSamples to 0:\n\n```go\ns.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n```\n\nThis is a critical bug because it doesn't account for samples that might still be in the old queues being flushed! Here's the sequence:1. Old shards have, say, 100 samples pending\n2. pendingSamples = 100\n3. updateShardsLoop detects it needs to reshard and sends new number to reshardChan\n4. reshardLoop calls stop() which closes softShutdown and flushes\n5. But before all samples are sent, reshardLoop also calls start() with new numShards\n6. start() sets pendingSamples = 0 (line 1241)\n7. Now the old shard goroutines that are still running will call updateMetrics when they finish sending\n8. updateMetrics does pendingSamples.Sub(sampleCount), which will decrement from 0 or go negativeOR, more likely:1. New samples start being enqueued to new shards while old shards are still flushing\n2. Old shards eventually finish and send their samples via updateMetrics which decrements from an incorrect baseline\n\nBut wait, the issue says \"some shards have prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending stuck at >0\". This suggests the samples are not being sent at all, not that the metric is negative.\n\nLet me reconsider the race condition. The critical insight is in the reshardLoop (lines 1184-1199):\n\n```go\nfunc (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n    defer t.wg.Done()\n    \n    for {\n        select {\n        case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n            // We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n            // flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n            // order.\n            t.shards.stop()  // <-- Waits for all old shards to flush\n            t.shards.start(numShards)  // <-- Starts new shards, RESETS pendingSamples\n        case <-t.quit:\n            return\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe comment claims that stop() waits for all samples to be completely flushed before start() is called, which would make resetting pendingSamples safe. But if there's a gap between when stop() returns and when the final updateMetrics calls complete, or if updateMetrics calls are still in flight when start() resets the counter, the metric becomes unreliable.\n\nHowever, there's a bigger issue: if FlushAndShutdown times out and triggers a hard shutdown instead (line 1293-1294), the partial batch gets discarded without being sent. func(int) error, onRetry func()) error {\n1982: \tbackoff := t.cfg.MinBackoff\n1983: \tsleepDuration := model.Duration(0)\n1984: \ttry := 0\n1985: \n1986: \tfor {\n1987: \t\tselect {\n1988: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n1989: \t\t\treturn ctx.Err()\n1990: \t\tdefault:\n1991: \t\t}\n1992: \n1993: \t\terr := attempt(try)\n1994: \n1995: \t\tif err == nil {\n1996: \t\t\treturn nil\n1997: \t\t}\n1998: \n1999: \t\t// If the error is unrecoverable, we should not retry.\n2000: \t\tvar backoffErr RecoverableError\n2001: \t\tif !errors.As(err, &backoffErr) {\n2002: \t\t\treturn err\n2003: \t\t}\n2004: \n2005: \t\tsleepDuration = backoff\n2006: \t\tswitch {\n2007: \t\tcase backoffErr.retryAfter > 0:\n2008: \t\t\tsleepDuration = backoffErr.retryAfter\n2009: \t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Retrying after duration specified by Retry-After header\", \"duration\", sleepDuration)\n2010: \t\tcase backoffErr.retryAfter < 0:\n2011: \t\t\tt.logger.Debug(\"retry-after cannot be in past, retrying using default backoff mechanism\")\n2012: \t\t}\n2013: \n2014: \t\t// We should never reshard for a recoverable error; increasing shards could\n2015: \t\t// make the problem worse, particularly if we're getting rate limited.\n2016: \t\t//\n2017: \t\t// reshardDisableTimestamp holds the unix timestamp until which resharding\n2018: \t\t// is disabled. We'll update that timestamp if the period we were just told\n2019: \t\t// to sleep for is newer than the existing disabled timestamp.\n2020: \t\treshardWaitPeriod := time.Now().Add(time.Duration(sleepDuration) * 2)\n2021: \t\tif oldTS, updated := setAtomicToNewer(&t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp, reshardWaitPeriod.Unix()); updated {\n2022: \t\t\t// If the old timestamp was in the past, then resharding was previously\n2023: \t\t\t// enabled. We want to track the time where it initially got disabled for\n2024: \t\t\t// logging purposes.\n2025: \t\t\tdisableTime := time.Now().Unix()\n2026: \t\t\tif oldTS < disableTime {\n2027: \t\t\t\tt.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Store(disableTime)\n2028: \t\t\t}\n2029: \t\t}\n2030: \n2031: \t\tselect {\n2032: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n2033: \t\tcase <-time.After(time.Duration(sleepDuration)):\n2034: \t\t}\n2035: \n2036: \t\t// If we make it this far, we've encountered a recoverable error and will retry.\n2037: \t\tonRetry()\n2038: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Failed to send batch, retrying\", \"err\", err)\n2039: \n2040: \t\tbackoff = min(sleepDuration*2, t.cfg.MaxBackoff)\n2041: \n2042: \t\ttry++\n2043: \t}\n2044: }\n2045: \n2046: // setAtomicToNewer atomically sets a value to the newer int64 between itself\n2047: // and the provided newValue argument. setAtomicToNewer returns whether the\n2048: // atomic value was updated and what the previous value was.\n2049: func setAtomicToNewer(value *atomic.Int64, newValue int64) (previous int64, updated bool) {\n2050: \tfor {\n2051: \t\tcurrent := value.Load()\n2052: \t\tif current >= newValue {\n2053: \t\t\t// If the current stored value is newer than newValue; abort.\n2054: \t\t\treturn current, false\n2055: \t\t}\n2056: \n2057: \t\t// Try to swap the value. If the atomic value has changed, we loop back to\n2058: \t\t// the beginning until we've successfully swapped out the value or the\n2059: \t\t// value stored in it is newer than newValue.\n2060: \t\tif value.CompareAndSwap(current, newValue) {\n2061: \t\t\treturn current, true\n2062: \t\t}\n2063: \t}\n2064: }\n2065: \n2066: func buildTimeSeries(timeSeries []prompb.TimeSeries, filter func(prompb.TimeSeries) bool) (int64, int64, []prompb.TimeSeries, int, int, int) {\n2067: \tvar highest int64\n2068: \tvar lowest int64\n2069: \tvar droppedSamples, droppedExemplars, droppedHistograms {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Lk144AVGaLQKtX7YEuyEwo","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01Kjme1YDkAHbzthLEiCVjYZ","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nResharding of remote-write queues causes samples to stall because of a race condition where in-flight samples don't properly update the `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` metric when the shard context is cancelled during resharding. Samples that fail to send due to context cancellation bypass the metrics update, leaving the pending counter stuck at a non-zero value while new samples accumulate.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### The Race Condition: Lost Metric Updates During Resharding\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n\nThe root cause involves a timing race between sample metrics tracking and context cancellation during resharding:\n\n1. **Samples Enqueued & Metric Incremented** (lines 1320-1327):\n   - When `enqueue()` adds a sample, it increments `pendingSamples.Inc()`\n   - These samples are queued in the old shard's `queue.batch` or sent directly\n\n2. **Resharding Triggered** (lines 1057-1082 `updateShardsLoop`):\n   - The `calculateDesiredShards()` function detects need to reshard\n   - Sends new shard count to `reshardChan`\n\n3. **Context Cancellation During Send** (lines 1184-1199 `reshardLoop`):\n   - `stop()` is called, which closes `softShutdown` and calls `hardShutdown()`\n   - `hardShutdown()` cancels the context for all active shard goroutines\n   - `start()` resets `pendingSamples` to 0 (line 1241)\n\n4. **Lost Metric Updates** (lines 1789-1792, 1911-1914):\n   ```go\n   if errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {\n       // When there is resharding, we cancel the context for this queue, which means the data is not sent.\n       // So we exit early to not update the metrics.\n       return accumulatedStats, err\n   }\n   ```\n   - **Critical Bug**: Samples in `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` that receive `context.Canceled` exit early WITHOUT calling `updateMetrics()`\n   - These samples already incremented `pendingSamples` during enqueue\n   - Their metrics are never decremented, leaving `pendingSamples` stuck >0\n\n### Why It's Intermittent\n\nThe race condition is intermittent because:\n\n1. **Timing Dependent**: The bug only manifests if samples are in-flight (inside `sendSamplesWithBackoff()`) when `hardShutdown()` is called\n2. **Network Latency**: Slower remote-write endpoints increase the window when samples are in-flight\n3. **Queue Backpressure**: High sample ingestion rate means more samples are likely to be in-flight during resharding\n4. **Batch Boundaries**: Samples at batch boundaries have different timing characteristics\n\n### Secondary Issue: Metrics Reset\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1241`\n```go\ns.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n```\n\nWhen `start()` initializes new shards, it unconditionally resets `pendingSamples` to 0. This assumes all old shards have finished flushing, but:\n- If `stop()` times out with a hard shutdown, samples may still be in-flight\n- Old shard goroutines may still be executing `updateMetrics()`\n- These updates would then decrement from 0, creating negative values or metric inconsistencies\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Code References\n\n1. **Sample Enqueue** (queue_manager.go:1320-1327):\n   - `pendingSamples.Inc()` called for every enqueued sample\n   - Tracked per shard in `enqueuedSamples` (line 1327)\n\n2. **Context Cancellation in Resharding** (queue_manager.go:1563-1578):\n   - When `ctx.Done()` (hard shutdown) is triggered, samples are dropped\n   - Metrics ARE properly updated in this path\n\n3. **Send Failure Path - NO Metrics Update** (queue_manager.go:1789-1792, 1911-1914):\n   - `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` returns early on `context.Canceled`\n   - Does NOT call `updateMetrics()` to decrement `pendingSamples`\n   - Only `updateMetrics()` decrements the pending counters (queue_manager.go:1689)\n\n4. **Hard Shutdown Trigger** (queue_manager.go:1269-1305):\n   - `stop()` closes `softShutdown` and calls `hardShutdown()`\n   - Waits with timeout for queues to flush\n   - Times out and cancels context if not done quickly enough\n\n5. **Bugfix References** (CHANGELOG.md):\n   - Line 925: \"[BUGFIX] Remote-write: Fix deadlock between adding to queue and getting batch. #10395\"\n   - Line 451: \"[ENHANCEMENT] Remote Write: Disable resharding during active retry backoffs #13562\"\n   - Line 1457: \"[BUGFIX] Remote Write: Fixed blocked resharding edge case. #7122\"\n\n### Metric That Would Confirm Issue\n\nCheck these diagnostic metrics:\n1. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{remote_name=\"...\"}` - stuck >0\n2. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - should increase on hard shutdown\n3. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` - may not increment if metrics update is skipped\n4. Log messages: \"Resharding queues\", \"Resharding done\" - timing relative to stuck pending samples\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Primary Components\n- **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`** (core resharding logic)\n  - `QueueManager.reshardLoop()` (lines 1184-1199)\n  - `shards.stop()` (lines 1269-1305)\n  - `shards.start()` (lines 1237-1266)\n  - `shards.runShard()` (lines 1491-1602)\n  - `shards.sendSamplesWithBackoff()` (lines 1698-1808)\n  - `shards.sendV2SamplesWithBackoff()` (lines 1811-1920)\n  - `shards.updateMetrics()` (lines 1661-1695)\n\n### Affected Packages\n- `storage/remote` - remote write queue management\n- `config` - QueueConfig with MinShards/MaxShards settings\n- Metrics exported via `prometheus` client library\n\n### Related Tests\n- `TestReshardRaceWithStop()` (queue_manager_test.go:553) - stress tests resharding race\n- `TestQueue_FlushAndShutdownDoesNotDeadlock()` (queue_manager_test.go:1787) - deadlock prevention\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Primary Fix**: Ensure metrics are updated for all samples regardless of how they exit\n\n1. **For samples in-flight during context cancellation**:\n   - Track samples that enter `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` but don't complete\n   - On context cancellation, still call `updateMetrics()` with the correct sample count\n   - Mark these as \"failed\" in metrics but ensure `pendingSamples` is decremented\n\n2. **For pending samples tracking**:\n   - Don't reset `pendingSamples.Set(0)` in `start()`\n   - Instead, only update it after all old shards have fully completed\n   - Consider adding synchronization between old shard completion and new shard initialization\n\n3. **Prevent the race entirely**:\n   - Ensure `stop()` fully completes before `start()` is called\n   - Add assertion that all old shards have finished before resetting metrics\n   - Consider tracking in-flight sample count separately\n\n### Diagnostic Steps to Confirm Root Cause\n\n1. **During resharding, check**:\n   - Are samples stuck in pending while no new sends are attempted?\n   - Do logs show \"Resharding done\" followed by metrics stuck >0?\n   - Is there correlation with network latency or remote endpoint issues?\n\n2. **Check metrics timeline**:\n   ```promql\n   rate(prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending[30s])\n   # Should be 0 if no new samples. Positive value indicates traffic.\n   ```\n\n3. **Check shard transitions**:\n   ```promql\n   prometheus_remote_storage_num_shards  # Changes during resharding\n   ```\n\n4. **Enable debug logging**:\n   - Set log level to debug to capture detailed resharding timestamps\n   - Correlate with exact moment `pendingSamples` gets stuck\n\n5. **Test with network latency**:\n   - Introduce artificial latency to remote endpoint\n   - Trigger target discovery changes to force resharding\n   - Observe if `samples_pending` gets stuck during resharding\n\n### Prevention\n\nUntil fixed:\n- Avoid frequent target discovery changes that trigger resharding\n- Increase `flushDeadline` in queue config to allow longer for samples to flush\n- Use fixed number of shards if possible (set `min_shards` = `max_shards`)\n- Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` for stuck values post-resharding\n\n## Additional Notes\n\nThe issue is particularly problematic because:\n1. Samples that fail to send due to context cancellation bypass the metrics update, leaving the pending counter stuck at a non-zero value while new samples accumulate.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### The Race Condition: Lost Metric Updates During Resharding\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n\nThe root cause involves a timing race between sample metrics tracking and context cancellation during resharding:\n\n1. **Samples Enqueued & Metric Incremented** (lines 1320-1327):\n   - When `enqueue()` adds a sample, it increments `pendingSamples.Inc()`\n   - These samples are queued in the old shard's `queue.batch` or sent directly\n\n2. **Resharding Triggered** (lines 1057-1082 `updateShardsLoop`):\n   - The `calculateDesiredShards()` function detects need to reshard\n   - Sends new shard count to `reshardChan`\n\n3. **Context Cancellation During Send** (lines 1184-1199 `reshardLoop`):\n   - `stop()` is called, which closes `softShutdown` and calls `hardShutdown()`\n   - `hardShutdown()` cancels the context for all active shard goroutines\n   - `start()` resets `pendingSamples` to 0 (line 1241)\n\n4. **Lost Metric Updates** (lines 1789-1792, 1911-1914):\n   ```go\n   if errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {\n       // When there is resharding, we cancel the context for this queue, which means the data is not sent.\n       // So we exit early to not update the metrics.\n       return accumulatedStats, err\n   }\n   ```\n   - **Critical Bug**: Samples in `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` that receive `context.Canceled` exit early WITHOUT calling `updateMetrics()`\n   - These samples already incremented `pendingSamples` during enqueue\n   - Their metrics are never decremented, leaving `pendingSamples` stuck >0\n\n### Why It's Intermittent\n\nThe race condition is intermittent because:\n\n1. **Timing Dependent**: The bug only manifests if samples are in-flight (inside `sendSamplesWithBackoff()`) when `hardShutdown()` is called\n2. **Network Latency**: Slower remote-write endpoints increase the window when samples are in-flight\n3. **Queue Backpressure**: High sample ingestion rate means more samples are likely to be in-flight during resharding\n4. **Batch Boundaries**: Samples at batch boundaries have different timing characteristics\n\n### Secondary Issue: Metrics Reset\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1241`\n```go\ns.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n```\n\nWhen `start()` initializes new shards, it unconditionally resets `pendingSamples` to 0. This assumes all old shards have finished flushing, but:\n- If `stop()` times out with a hard shutdown, samples may still be in-flight\n- Old shard goroutines may still be executing `updateMetrics()`\n- These updates would then decrement from 0, creating negative values or metric inconsistencies\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Code References\n\n1. **Sample Enqueue** (queue_manager.go:1320-1327):\n   - `pendingSamples.Inc()` called for every enqueued sample\n   - Tracked per shard in `enqueuedSamples` (line 1327)\n\n2. **Context Cancellation in Resharding** (queue_manager.go:1563-1578):\n   - When `ctx.Done()` (hard shutdown) is triggered, samples are dropped\n   - Metrics ARE properly updated in this path\n\n3. **Send Failure Path - NO Metrics Update** (queue_manager.go:1789-1792, 1911-1914):\n   - `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` returns early on `context.Canceled`\n   - Does NOT call `updateMetrics()` to decrement `pendingSamples`\n   - Only `updateMetrics()` decrements the pending counters (queue_manager.go:1689)\n\n4. **Hard Shutdown Trigger** (queue_manager.go:1269-1305):\n   - `stop()` closes `softShutdown` and calls `hardShutdown()`\n   - Waits with timeout for queues to flush\n   - Times out and cancels context if not done quickly enough\n\n5. **Bugfix References** (CHANGELOG.md):\n   - Line 925: \"[BUGFIX] Remote-write: Fix deadlock between adding to queue and getting batch. #10395\"\n   - Line 451: \"[ENHANCEMENT] Remote Write: Disable resharding during active retry backoffs #13562\"\n   - Line 1457: \"[BUGFIX] Remote Write: Fixed blocked resharding edge case. #7122\"\n\n### Metric That Would Confirm Issue\n\nCheck these diagnostic metrics:\n1. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{remote_name=\"...\"}` - stuck >0\n2. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - should increase on hard shutdown\n3. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` - may not increment if metrics update is skipped\n4. Log messages: \"Resharding queues\", \"Resharding done\" - timing relative to stuck pending samples\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Primary Components\n- **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`** (core resharding logic)\n  - `QueueManager.reshardLoop()` (lines 1184-1199)\n  - `shards.stop()` (lines 1269-1305)\n  - `shards.start()` (lines 1237-1266)\n  - `shards.runShard()` (lines 1491-1602)\n  - `shards.sendSamplesWithBackoff()` (lines 1698-1808)\n  - `shards.sendV2SamplesWithBackoff()` (lines 1811-1920)\n  - `shards.updateMetrics()` (lines 1661-1695)\n\n### Affected Packages\n- `storage/remote` - remote write queue management\n- `config` - QueueConfig with MinShards/MaxShards settings\n- Metrics exported via `prometheus` client library\n\n### Related Tests\n- `TestReshardRaceWithStop()` (queue_manager_test.go:553) - stress tests resharding race\n- `TestQueue_FlushAndShutdownDoesNotDeadlock()` (queue_manager_test.go:1787) - deadlock prevention\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Primary Fix**: Ensure metrics are updated for all samples regardless of how they exit\n\n1. **For samples in-flight during context cancellation**:\n   - Track samples that enter `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` but don't complete\n   - On context cancellation, still call `updateMetrics()` with the correct sample count\n   - Mark these as \"failed\" in metrics but ensure `pendingSamples` is decremented\n\n2. **For pending samples tracking**:\n   - Don't reset `pendingSamples.Set(0)` in `start()`\n   - Instead, only update it after all old shards have fully completed\n   - Consider adding synchronization between old shard completion and new shard initialization\n\n3. **Prevent the race entirely**:\n   - Ensure `stop()` fully completes before `start()` is called\n   - Add assertion that all old shards have finished before resetting metrics\n   - Consider tracking in-flight sample count separately\n\n### Diagnostic Steps to Confirm Root Cause\n\n1. **During resharding, check**:\n   - Are samples stuck in pending while no new sends are attempted?\n   - Do logs show \"Resharding done\" followed by metrics stuck >0?\n   - Is there correlation with network latency or remote endpoint issues?\n\n2. **Check metrics timeline**:\n   ```promql\n   rate(prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending[30s])\n   # Should be 0 if no new samples. Positive value indicates traffic.\n   ```\n\n3. **Check shard transitions**:\n   ```promql\n   prometheus_remote_storage_num_shards  # Changes during resharding\n   ```\n\n4. **Enable debug logging**:\n   - Set log level to debug to capture detailed resharding timestamps\n   - Correlate with exact moment `pendingSamples` gets stuck\n\n5. **Test with network latency**:\n   - Introduce artificial latency to remote endpoint\n   - Trigger target discovery changes to force resharding\n   - Observe if `samples_pending` gets stuck during resharding\n\n### Prevention\n\nUntil fixed:\n- Avoid frequent target discovery changes that trigger resharding\n- Increase `flushDeadline` in queue config to allow longer for samples to flush\n- Use fixed number of shards if possible (set `min_shards` = `max_shards`)\n- Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` for stuck values post-resharding\n\n## Additional Notes\n\nThe issue is particularly problematic because:\n1. It's a silent failure - no error is logged when metrics become inconsistent\n2. Samples aren't actually lost (they're sent), but the metric makes it appear they are\n3. This breaks Prometheus's remote-write reliability guarantees at the observability level\n4.
